< review>
We did not want toxic chemicals pumped into the home, nor put into the ground under and around our home. The tenting process would have wiped out a lot of landscaping near the home. The house is 96 years old with a steeply pitched roof and there would have been a considerable extra charge with the dangerous task of getting the tent on our roof.We had a heat treatment company come out but were told that process can warp your floorboards and cause damage to other items in your home.

We were also told by a reputable termite company that the tenting process is a "brutal process" on any home but especially ours.

Enter Xtermite and their orange oil method. Takes a few hours, you don't need to leave the home, only leaves behind orange scent and a few targeted holes where they need to inject their organic sprays. Arguably it is not as effective as gas and injections of a termicide but it is good enough. AND, they have an outstanding program where they will come to the home and retreat any hot spots, free, for three years. AND, they do a once per year free inspection.

I highly recommend you ask for Neecole Brooks to come inspect your home. This guy knows his stuff, will answer every single question you have with patience and decades of experience.</review>

I called Xtermite to fix my termite problem because my dad used them for many years and he says many good things about their service.  I was impressed with the inspection process as it looked very thorough, the inspector went into the attic above the garage and house and looked at the problem areas that I could see on the roof outside the second story bedroom  plus he saw other problems that I did not see.  This was a big improvement from the last inspector from another company who simply walked around the house with a clipboard without a ladder, and not even tapping on eaves, etc to determine termite damage.  The technician came a few days later and spent about five hours treating the house.  However, some of the orange treatment dripped onto several of my plants outside, and especially one appeared to be very damaged.  The technician should have covered the plants to protect them.  I called Xtermite about this and sent photos of the damaged plants and a few days later, I got a call that they acknowledged their negligence in not protecting the plants and promised to extend my warranty another six months and to compensate for the plant if it dies.  This satisfied me, and I think that the orange treatment will be very effective.  I will be looking very hard for any termite activity  and am reassured that Xtermite will come and treat any problems I see.  As it stands for now, I am satisfied with their service.<//Review>

<Review>It's morning. I need a bagel and a cup of dark-roast coffee. This is serious.  Please understand, toasted bread, baguette, even challah are ineffective substitutes.  It has to be firm, with a real crust. If fresh, don't toast. If not, toast. Sometimes life is not perfect.

The best bagel I have devoured was in a delicatessen, located in Golders Green, London, England. My favorite in the United States is Bethesda Bagel in Bethesda, Maryland.

The Bagel Street Cafe, part of a limited chain, is a small, well-run bagel shop offering a dozen flavors of New York style boiled bagels.  (After bagel dough is formed, it is allowed to rest a bit, then dropped into boiling water, quickly removed and baked.)

The bagels are just out of the oven, fresh.  I ordered my traditional vegan breakfast, rye bagel (not toasted), tomatoes, cucumbers and capers. No vegan cream cheese was available. Their quality is above average.

The French roast coffee was strong and delicious.

There is a limited selection of pastry, salads, and a large selection of soft drinks.

The Bagel Street is located in the center of a upscale shopping complex. Both indoor and Patio seating is available. Everything is wheelchair accessible. Closed on Sundays.

As the Master explained, "Life is like a bagel. Focus on the hole and you won't enjoy the crust."<//Review><date>1548105320123<//date>< gmapID>

I occasionally shopped here in the past and noticed the slow change to an "international" food emporium.
The store is huge and has a warehouse feel.

They have a good variety of pakistani indian groceries, however produce is hardly ever fresh and the cleanliness can be improved hugely. The meat prices are competitive.</text>

<resp>None< /resp>< text>
The grocery store is super convenient for many because of it's location but has a few strengths and weaknesses.  The main strengths are that you can find lots of good meat that you can't find in other grocery stores.  You'l find lamb, goat, etc, here so if you're making Indian curries this can be a solid spot for those meats.  There are a lot of Indian frozen foods too such as naan and rotis too.  They have indian and middle eastern spice mixes, paneer and sweets, and lots of indian snacks.  The downsides are mostly that the lines to check out are usually long and slow, and there's no express line so for a couple items you might have to wait a while.  Your best bet is to go during off hours and grab what you need.</text>
